with, at\n * your election, the \"Elastic License 2.0\", the \"GNU Affero General Public\n * License v3.0 only\", or the \"Server Side Public License, v 1\".\n */\n\npackage org.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.allocation.decider;\n\nimport org.apache.logging.log4j.LogManager;\nimport org.apache.logging.log4j.Logger;\nimport org.elasticsearch.cluster.metadata.IndexMetadata;\nimport org.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.RoutingNode;\nimport org.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.ShardRouting;\nimport org.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.allocation.RoutingAllocation;\nimport org.elasticsearch.common.settings.ClusterSettings;\nimport org.elasticsearch.common.settings.Setting;\nimport org.elasticsearch.common.settings.Setting.Property;\nimport org.elasticsearch.common.settings.Settings;\n\nimport java.util.List;\n\n/**\n * {@link AllocationDecider} that implements priority-based shard allocation constraints.\n *\n * <p>\n * This decider allows Elasticsearch to preferentially allocate shards from high-priority\n * indices to high-performance (premium-tier) nodes, while gracefully degrading to\n * standard-tier nodes when necessary.\n * </p>\n *\n * <h2>Decision Logic</h2>\n *\n * For each shard allocation attempt:\n * <ol>\n *   <li>If priority allocation is disabled, return {@link Decision#ALWAYS} (no constraints)</li>\n *   <li>Retrieve the index's priority level from its metadata</li>\n *   <li>Classify the target node as premium or standard tier</li>\n *   <li>Apply decision rules based on priority and tier:\n *     <ul>\n *       <li>High priority (>= threshold) on premium tier \u2192 {@link Decision#YES}</li>\n *       <li>High priority (>= threshold) on standard tier \u2192 {@link Decision#THROTTLE}\n *           (soft constraint; allow but prefer premium)</li>\n *       <li>Low priority (< threshold) on any tier \u2192 {@link Decision#YES}</li>\n *     </ul>\n *   </li>\n * </ol>\n * </p>\n *\n * <h2>Configuration</h2>\n *\n * Enable/disable the decider (cluster-level):\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled: true\n * </pre>\n *\n * Define premium tier node attributes:\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers: [premium, hot]\n * </pre>\n *\n * Set priority threshold for soft constraints:\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold: 70\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h2>Index Configuration</h2>\n *\n * Set index priority (0-100, default 50):\n * <pre>\n * PUT /myindex/_settings\n * {\n *   \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 100\n * }\n * </pre>\n *\n * Node tier classification (set in elasticsearch.yml or via node API):\n * <pre>\n * node.attr.allocation_tier: premium  # or \"standard\", \"basic\", etc.\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h2>Interaction with Other Deciders</h2>\n *\n * PriorityAllocationDecider is typically placed in the decider chain after:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>EnableAllocationDecider (check if allocation is enabled)</li>\n *   <li>DiskThresholdDecider (check if node has disk space)</li>\n *   <li>AwarenessAllocationDecider (check rack/zone constraints)</li>\n *   <li>FilterAllocationDecider (check include/exclude/require filters)</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * This ensures that hard constraints (disk space, awareness) take precedence over\n * priority preferences.\n *\n * <h2>Examples</h2>\n *\n * <h3>Example 1: High-Priority Index Prefers Premium Nodes</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Cluster:\n *   - node-1: tier=premium (100MB free)\n *   - node-2: tier=standard (500MB free)\n *\n * Index: critical-app\n *   - priority=90\n *   - decision for node-1: YES (high priority + premium tier)\n *   - decision for node-2: THROTTLE (high priority + standard tier; suboptimal)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates to node-1 (preferred)\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h3>Example 2: Low-Priority Index No Preference</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Index: cache-index\n *   - priority=10\n *   - decision for any node: YES (below threshold)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates based on balanced allocation (no priority constraint)\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h3>Example 3: Degradation When Premium Nodes Full</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Cluster:\n *   - node-1: tier=premium (FULL - disk threshold breach)\n *   - node-2: tier=standard (500MB free)\n *\n * Index: critical-app\n *   - priority=90\n *   - decision for node-1: NO (DiskThresholdDecider blocks)\n *   - decision for node-2: THROTTLE (high priority but suboptimal tier)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates to node-2 (graceful degradation)\n * </pre>\n *\n * @see PriorityShardsAllocator\n * @see AllocationDecider\n * @see Decision\n */\npublic class PriorityAllocationDecider extends AllocationDecider {\n\n    private static final Logger logger = LogManager.getLogger(PriorityAllocationDecider.class);\n\n    public static final String NAME = \"priority_allocation\";\n\n    /**\n     * Cluster-level setting to enable/disable priority-aware allocation constraints.\n     * When disabled, this decider returns {@link Decision#ALWAYS} for all decisions.\n     * Default: true\n     */\n    public static final Setting<Boolean> CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_ENABLED = Setting.boolSetting(\n        \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled\",\n        true,\n        Property.Dynamic,\n        Property.NodeScope\n    );\n\n    /**\n     * Cluster-level setting listing the node tier names considered \"premium\".\n     * Nodes with the `allocation_tier` attribute matching one of these values\n     * are classified as premium and receive priority preference for high-priority shards.\n     * Default: [\"premium\"]\n     *\n     * Example:\n     * <pre>\n     * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers: [premium, hot]\n     * </pre>\n     */\n    public static final Setting<List<String>> CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_PREMIUM_TIERS = Setting.stringListSetting(\n        \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers\",\n        java.util.List.of(\"premium\"),\n        Property.Dynamic,\n        Property.NodeScope\n    );\n\n    /**\n     * Cluster-level setting specifying the priority threshold above which\n     * the decider applies soft constraints (THROTTLE) for standard-tier nodes.\n     * Shards from indices with priority >= this threshold prefer premium nodes,\n     * but can still allocate to standard nodes (via THROTTLE decision).\n     *\n     * Range: 0-100\n     * Default: 70\n     *\n     * Example:\n     * <pre>\n     * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold: 70\n     * </pre>\n     */\n    public static final Setting<Integer> CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_THRESHOLD = Setting.intSetting(\n        \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold\",\n        70,\n        0,\n        100,\n        Property.Dynamic,\n        Property.NodeScope\n    );\n\n    // Volatile fields for dynamic configuration updates\n    private volatile boolean priorityAllocationEnabled;\n    private volatile List<String> premiumTiers;\n    private volatile int priorityThreshold;\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a new PriorityAllocationDecider with default settings.\n     */\n    public PriorityAllocationDecider() {\n        this.priorityAllocationEnabled = true;\n        this.premiumTiers = java.util.List.of(\"premium\");\n        this.priorityThreshold = 70;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a new PriorityAllocationDecider with settings from the provided\n     * configuration. Registers dynamic setting listeners for configuration updates.\n     *\n     * @param settings the node settings (unused; settings come from clusterSettings)\n     * @param clusterSettings the cluster settings to watch for updates\n     */\n    public PriorityAllocationDecider(Settings settings, ClusterSettings clusterSettings) {\n        // Initialize from cluster settings\n        this.priorityAllocationEnabled = CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_ENABLED.get(settings);\n        this.premiumTiers = CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_PREMIUM_TIERS.get(settings);\n        this.priorityThreshold = CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_THRESHOLD.get(settings);\n\n        // Register listeners for dynamic updates\n        clusterSettings.addSettingsUpdateConsumer(\n            CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_ENABLED,\n            this::setPriorityAllocationEnabled\n        );\n        clusterSettings.addSettingsUpdateConsumer(\n            CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_PREMIUM_TIERS,\n            this::setPremiumTiers\n        );\n        clusterSettings.addSettingsUpdateConsumer(\n            CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_THRESHOLD,\n            this::setPriorityThreshold\n        );\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decides whether a shard can be allocated to a specific node.\n     *\n     * <p>\n     * Decision logic:\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>If priority allocation is disabled, return YES (always allow)</li>\n     *   <li>Get index priority from metadata (default 50 if not set)</li>\n     *   <li>Determine if node is premium tier</li>\n     *   <li>Apply priority-based constraints:\n     *     <ul>\n     *       <li>If priority >= threshold AND node is premium: YES</li>\n     *       <li>If priority >= threshold AND node is standard: THROTTLE (soft constraint)</li>\n     *       <li>If priority < threshold: YES (no constraint)</li>\n     *     </ul>\n     *   </li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @param shardRouting the shard being allocated\n     * @param node the target node for allocation\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @return the allocation decision (YES, THROTTLE, or NO)\n     */\n    @Override\n    public Decision canAllocate(ShardRouting shardRouting, RoutingNode node, RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n        if (!priorityAllocationEnabled) {\n            return Decision.ALWAYS; // Feature disabled; no constraints\n        }\n\n        // Extract index priority\n        IndexMetadata indexMetadata = allocation.metadata().getIndexSafe(shardRouting.index());\n        int indexPriority = getIndexPriority(indexMetadata);\n\n        // Check if index priority warrants tier-based constraints\n        if (indexPriority < priorityThreshold) {\n            // Low priority; no constraint\n            if (logger.isTraceEnabled()) {\n                logger.trace(\n                    \"Shard [{}] has priority {} (below threshold {}); no priority-based constraint\",\n                    shardRouting.shardId(),\n                    indexPriority,\n                    priorityThreshold\n                );\n            }\n            return Decision.ALWAYS;\n        }\n\n        // High priority; check node tier\n        boolean isNodePremium = isNodePremiumTier(node, allocation);\n        if (isNodePremium) {\n            // Preferred allocation\n            if (logger.isTraceEnabled()) {\n                logger.trace(\n                    \"Shard [{}] has high priority {}; allocating to premium node [{}]\",\n                    shardRouting.shardId(),\n                    indexPriority,\n                    node.nodeId()\n                );\n            }\n            return allocation.decision(\n                Decision.YES,\n                NAME,\n                \"shard [%s] has high priority [%d]; premium tier node [%s]\",\n                shardRouting.shardId(),\n                indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId()\n            );\n        } else {\n            // Suboptimal allocation; allow with THROTTLE (soft constraint)\n            if (logger.isTraceEnabled()) {\n                logger.trace(\n                    \"Shard [{}] has high priority {} but standard node [{}]; throttling\",\n                    shardRouting.shardId(),\n                    indexPriority,\n                    node.nodeId()\n                );\n            }\n            return allocation.decision(\n                Decision.THROTTLE,\n                NAME,\n                \"shard [%s] has high priority [%d]; standard tier node [%s] (prefer premium)\",\n                shardRouting.shardId(),\n                indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId()\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decides whether a shard can remain on its current node.\n     * Uses the same logic as canAllocate() since priority constraints apply equally.\n     *\n     * @param indexMetadata the index metadata\n     * @param shardRouting the shard currently residing on the node\n     * @param node the node where the shard currently resides\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @return the allocation decision\n     */\n    @Override\n    public Decision canRemain(\n        IndexMetadata indexMetadata,\n        ShardRouting shardRouting,\n        RoutingNode node,\n        RoutingAllocation allocation\n    ) {\n        // For residency decisions, use the same priority constraints as allocation\n        // A high-priority shard may be encouraged to move to a premium node if\n        // it's currently on a standard node (handled via rebalancing, not here)\n        return canAllocate(shardRouting, node, allocation);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Extracts the priority value for an index from its metadata.\n     * Falls back to default priority if not explicitly shard allocation constraints.\n *\n * <p>\n * This decider allows Elasticsearch to preferentially allocate shards from high-priority\n * indices to high-performance (premium-tier) nodes, while gracefully degrading to\n * standard-tier nodes when necessary.\n * </p>\n *\n * <h2>Decision Logic</h2>\n *\n * For each shard allocation attempt:\n * <ol>\n *   <li>If priority allocation is disabled, return {@link Decision#ALWAYS} (no constraints)</li>\n *   <li>Retrieve the index's priority level from its metadata</li>\n *   <li>Classify the target node as premium or standard tier</li>\n *   <li>Apply decision rules based on priority and tier:\n *     <ul>\n *       <li>High priority (>= threshold) on premium tier \u2192 {@link Decision#YES}</li>\n *       <li>High priority (>= threshold) on standard tier \u2192 {@link Decision#THROTTLE}\n *           (soft constraint; allow but prefer premium)</li>\n *       <li>Low priority (< threshold) on any tier \u2192 {@link Decision#YES}</li>\n *     </ul>\n *   </li>\n * </ol>\n * </p>\n *\n * <h2>Configuration</h2>\n *\n * Enable/disable the decider (cluster-level):\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled: true\n * </pre>\n *\n * Define premium tier node attributes:\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers: [premium, hot]\n * </pre>\n *\n * Set priority threshold for soft constraints:\n * <pre>\n * cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold: 70\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h2>Index Configuration</h2>\n *\n * Set index priority (0-100, default 50):\n * <pre>\n * PUT /myindex/_settings\n * {\n *   \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 100\n * }\n * </pre>\n *\n * Node tier classification (set in elasticsearch.yml or via node API):\n * <pre>\n * node.attr.allocation_tier: premium  # or \"standard\", \"basic\", etc.\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h2>Interaction with Other Deciders</h2>\n *\n * PriorityAllocationDecider is typically placed in the decider chain after:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>EnableAllocationDecider (check if allocation is enabled)</li>\n *   <li>DiskThresholdDecider (check if node has disk space)</li>\n *   <li>AwarenessAllocationDecider (check rack/zone constraints)</li>\n *   <li>FilterAllocationDecider (check include/exclude/require filters)</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * This ensures that hard constraints (disk space, awareness) take precedence over\n * priority preferences.\n *\n * <h2>Examples</h2>\n *\n * <h3>Example 1: High-Priority Index Prefers Premium Nodes</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Cluster:\n *   - node-1: tier=premium (100MB free)\n *   - node-2: tier=standard (500MB free)\n *\n * Index: critical-app\n *   - priority=90\n *   - decision for node-1: YES (high priority + premium tier)\n *   - decision for node-2: THROTTLE (high priority + standard tier; suboptimal)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates to node-1 (preferred)\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h3>Example 2: Low-Priority Index No Preference</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Index: cache-index\n *   - priority=10\n *   - decision for any node: YES (below threshold)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates based on balanced allocation (no priority constraint)\n * </pre>\n *\n * <h3>Example 3: Degradation When Premium Nodes Full</h3>\n * <pre>\n * Cluster:\n *   - node-1: tier=premium (FULL - disk threshold breach)\n *   - node-2: tier=standard (500MB free)\n *\n * Index: critical-app\n *   - priority=90\n *   - decision for node-1: NO (DiskThresholdDecider blocks)\n *   - decision for node-2: THROTTLE (high priority but suboptimal tier)\n *\n * Result: Shard allocates to node-2 (graceful degradation)\n * </pre>\n *\n * @see PriorityShardsAllocator\n * @see AllocationDecider\n * @see Decision\n */\npublic class PriorityAllocationDecider this.priorityThreshold = CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_THRESHOLD.get(settings);\n\n        // Register listeners for dynamic updates\n        clusterSettings.addSettingsUpdateConsumer(\n CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_PREMIUM_TIERS,\n            this::setPremiumTiers\n        );\n        clusterSettings.addSettingsUpdateConsumer(\n            CLUSTER_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_THRESHOLD,\n            this::setPriorityThreshold\n        );\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decides whether a shard can be allocated to a specific node.\n     *\n     * <p>\n     * Decision logic:\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>If priority allocation is disabled, return YES (always allow)</li>\n     *   <li>Get index priority from metadata (default 50 if not set)</li>\n     *   <li>Determine if node is premium tier</li>\n     *   <li>Apply priority-based constraints:\n     *     <ul>\n     *       <li>If priority >= threshold AND node is premium:            shardRouting.shardId(),\n                indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId()\n            );\n        } else {\n            // Suboptimal allocation; allow with THROTTLE (soft constraint)\n            if (logger.isTraceEnabled()) {\n                logger.trace(\n                    \"Shard [{}] has high priority {} but standard node [{}]; throttling\",\n                    shardRouting.shardId(),\n                    indexPriority,\n                    node.nodeId()\n                );\n            }\n            return allocation.decision(\n                Decision.THROTTLE,\n                NAME,\n                \"shard [%s] has high priority [%d]; standard tier node [%s] (prefer premium)\",\n                shardRouting.shardId(),\n                indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId()\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decides whether a shard can remain on its current node.\n     * Uses the same logic as canAllocate() since priority constraints apply equally.\n     *\n     * @param indexMetadata the index metadata\n     * @param shardRouting the shard currently residing on the node\n     * @param node the node where the shard currently resides\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @return the allocation decision\n     */\n    @Override\n    public Decision canRemain(\n constraints as allocation\n        // A high-priority shard may be encouraged to move to a premium node if\n        // it's currently on a standard node (handled via rebalancing, not here)\n        return canAllocate(shardRouting, node, allocation);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Extracts the priority value for an index from its metadata.\n     * Falls back to default priority if not explicitly set.\n     *\n     * @param indexMetadata the index metadata\n     * @return the index priority (0-100), or default 50 if not set\n     */\n    private int getIndexPriority(IndexMetadata indexMetadata) {\n        try {\n            // TODO: Extract priority from index settings\n            // Pseudo-code:\n            // String priorityKey = PriorityShardsAllocator.INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY;\n            // return indexMetadata.getSettings().getAsInt(priorityKey, 50);\n            return 50; // placeholder\n        } catch {
  "content": "# Priority-Based Shard Allocation Strategy for Elasticsearch\n\n## Overview\n\nThis directory contains the design and skeleton implementation for a **priority-based shard allocation strategy** for Elasticsearch v8.17.0. The design enables critical indices to be preferentially placed on faster (premium-tier) nodes while maintaining graceful degradation when premium capacity is exhausted.\n\n## Deliverables\n\n### 1. **design_doc.md** - Comprehensive Design Document\n\nA complete design specification covering:\n\n- **Current Architecture Overview**: Detailed analysis of existing allocation framework\n  - ShardsAllocator interface and BalancedShardsAllocator implementation\n  - AllocationDecider base class and composition pattern\n  - Existing decider examples (DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider)\n\n- **Problem Statement**: Why priority-aware allocation is needed\n  - Current lack of performance-tier awareness\n  - Limitation in handling critical vs. non-critical indices\n\n- **Proposed Design**: Four-component solution\n  - `index.routing.allocation.priority` setting (0-100, default 50)\n  - `node.attr.allocation_tier` attribute (e.g., \"premium\", \"standard\")\n  - `PriorityAllocationDecider` - enforces priority constraints\n  - `PriorityShardsAllocator` - reorders shards by priority for allocation\n\n- **Integration Points**: How new components compose with existing allocation framework\n  - Placement in the decider chain\n  - Interaction with DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider, FilterAllocationDecider\n  - Backward compatibility and graceful degradation\n\n- **API Specification**: New settings and configuration\n  - Index settings: `index.routing.allocation.priority`\n  - Cluster settings: `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.*`\n  - Cluster Explain API enhancements\n\n- **Implementation Roadmap**: 4-phase development plan\n- **Behavior Examples**: Real-world scenarios with expected outcomes\n- **Testing Strategy**: Unit, integration, and chaos test plans\n- **References**: Links to relevant Elasticsearch source files\n\n**Key Design Principles**:\n1. Non-intrusive - integrates without major refactoring\n2. Composable - works alongside existing deciders\n3. Configurable - allows operator control and tuning\n4. Observable - clear logging and explain API output\n5. Safe - graceful degradation without data loss\n\n### 2. **PriorityShardsAllocator.java** - Skeleton Implementation\n\nA Java class implementing the `ShardsAllocator` interface that:\n\n- **Wraps BalancedShardsAllocator**: Delegates actual balancing decisions\n- **Sorts Shards by Priority**: Reorders unassigned shards queue (highest priority first)\n- **Supports Async Allocation**: Implements both sync and async allocation methods\n- **Dynamic Configuration**: Watches for runtime setting changes\n- **Graceful Error Handling**: Continues with standard allocation on errors\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `allocate(RoutingAllocation)` - sorts shards then delegates\n- `allocate(RoutingAllocation, ActionListener<Void>)` - async variant\n- `sortUnassignedShardsByPriority()` - reorders shard queue\n- `getIndexPriority()` - extracts priority from index metadata\n- `isNodePremiumTier()` - classifies node as premium/standard\n\n**Settings Exposed**:\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled` (Boolean, default: true)\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers` (List[String], default: [\"premium\"])\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold` (Integer 0-100, default: 70)\n\n### 3. **PriorityAllocationDecider.java** - Skeleton Implementation\n\nA Java class extending `AllocationDecider` that:\n\n- **Enforces Priority Constraints**: Returns YES/THROTTLE/NO based on priority and tier\n- **Decision Logic**:\n  - High-priority shard on premium node \u2192 YES\n  - High-priority shard on standard node \u2192 THROTTLE (soft constraint)\n  - Low-priority shard on any node \u2192 YES\n- **Composes with Other Deciders**: Fails fast on NO from other deciders\n- **Dynamic Configuration**: Watches for runtime setting changes\n- **Detailed Logging**: Trace-level logging for debugging allocation decisions\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `canAllocate(ShardRouting, RoutingNode, RoutingAllocation)` - main decision logic\n- `canRemain()` - uses same logic as canAllocate\n- `getIndexPriority()` - extracts priority from index metadata\n- `isNodePremiumTier()` - classifies node tier\n\n**Settings Exposed**:\n- Same as PriorityShardsAllocator\n\n## Architecture Diagram\n\n```\nAllocationService (orchestration)\n    \u2193\nShardsAllocator (pluggable)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 BalancedShardsAllocator (existing)\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 PriorityShardsAllocator (NEW)\n            \u2193\n        [reorder shards by priority]\n            \u2193\n        BalancedShardsAllocator.allocate()\n            \u2193\n        AllocationDeciders chain\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 EnableAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 DiskThresholdDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 AwarenessAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 FilterAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 PriorityAllocationDecider (NEW)\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 ... other deciders ...\n```\n\n## Design Highlights\n\n### 1. Non-Intrusive Integration\n\nThe design extends existing components rather than modifying them:\n- PriorityShardsAllocator wraps BalancedShardsAllocator (decorator pattern)\n- PriorityAllocationDecider extends AllocationDecider (template method pattern)\n- New settings follow Elasticsearch conventions\n\n### 2. Composability with Existing Deciders\n\nPriority constraints interact safely with other constraints:\n- **DiskThreshold** (hard constraint): Disk space checks take precedence\n- **Awareness** (hard constraint): Rack/zone distribution respected within priority preferences\n- **Filter** (hard constraint): Include/exclude/require filters applied first\n- **Priority** (soft constraint): THROTTLE signals preference, not requirement\n\n### 3. Graceful Degradation\n\nHigh-priority shards still allocate when premium nodes unavailable:\n- THROTTLE decision allows allocation to standard nodes\n- Falls back to standard balanced allocation\n- No starvation; all shards eventually allocate\n\n### 4. Dynamic Configuration\n\nAll settings are dynamic (cluster-scoped):\n- No cluster restart required to enable/disable\n- Can adjust premium tiers and thresholds at runtime\n- Easy A/B testing of configurations\n\n## Configuration Examples\n\n### Enable Priority Allocation\n\n```bash\nPUT /_cluster/settings\n{\n  \"persistent\": {\n    \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled\": true,\n    \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers\": [\"premium\", \"hot\"],\n    \"cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold\": 70\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Configure Node Tiers\n\nIn `elasticsearch.yml`:\n```yaml\n# Premium nodes (fast SSD, 256GB RAM)\nnode.name: premium-node-1\nnode.attr.allocation_tier: premium\n\n# Standard nodes (regular SSD, 64GB RAM)\nnode.name: standard-node-1\nnode.attr.allocation_tier: standard\n```\n\n### Set Index Priority\n\n```bash\nPUT /critical-app/_settings\n{\n  \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 100\n}\n\nPUT /cache-index/_settings\n{\n  \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 10\n}\n```\n\n## Usage Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Critical Application Index\n\n```\nIndex: critical-app\n- priority: 100 (highest)\n- 3 shards, 2 replicas each\n\nCluster:\n- 2 premium nodes (fast SSD, 256GB RAM)\n- 3 standard nodes (regular SSD, 64GB RAM)\n\nResult:\n- Primary shards prefer premium nodes\n- Replica shards distributed across both tiers\n- If premium nodes full, gracefully degrade to standard\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: Multi-Tier Allocation\n\n```\nIndices:\n- prod-primary (priority: 100)  \u2192 premium nodes\n- prod-replica (priority: 80)   \u2192 premium or standard\n- staging (priority: 40)        \u2192 any node\n- logs (priority: 10)           \u2192 standard nodes\n\nAllocation Strategy:\n1. Assign prod-primary shards first (highest priority)\n2. Fill premium nodes with prod-primary shards\n3. Assign prod-replica to remaining premium space + standard\n4. Assign staging to available space\n5. Pack logs into remaining capacity\n```\n\n## References to Elasticsearch Source\n\nThe skeleton code references these key Elasticsearch components:\n\n- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/allocator/ShardsAllocator.java`\n- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/decider/AwarenessAllocationDecider.java`\n- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/metadata/IndexMetadata.java`\n- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/common/settings/ClusterSettings.java`\n\n## Next Steps for Implementation\n\n### Phase 1: Foundation\n1. \u2705 Design document completed\n2. \u2705 Skeleton   "content": "# Priority-Based Shard Allocation Strategy for Elasticsearch\n\n## Overview\n\nThis directory contains the design and skeleton implementation for a **priority-based shard allocation strategy** for Elasticsearch v8.17.0. The design enables critical indices to be preferentially placed on faster (premium-tier) nodes while maintaining graceful degradation when premium capacity is exhausted.\n\n## Deliverables\n\n### 1. **design_doc.md** - Comprehensive Design Document\n\nA complete design specification covering:\n\n- **Current Architecture Overview**: Detailed analysis of existing allocation framework\n  - ShardsAllocator interface and BalancedShardsAllocator implementation\n  - AllocationDecider base class and composition pattern\n  - Existing decider examples (DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider)\n\n- **Problem Statement**: Why priority-aware allocation is needed\n  - Current lack of performance-tier awareness\n  - Limitation in handling critical vs. non-critical indices\n\n- **Proposed Design**: Four-component solution\n  - `index.routing.allocation.priority` setting (0-100, default 50)\n  - `node.attr.allocation_tier` attribute (e.g., \"premium\", \"standard\")\n  - `PriorityAllocationDecider` - enforces priority constraints\n  - `PriorityShardsAllocator` - reorders shards by priority for allocation\n\n- **Integration Points**: How new components compose with existing allocation framework\n  - Placement in the decider chain\n  - Interaction with DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider, FilterAllocationDecider\n  - Backward compatibility and graceful degradation\n\n- **API Specification**: New settings and configuration\n  - Index settings: `index.routing.allocation.priority`\n  - Cluster settings: `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.*`\n  - Cluster Explain API enhancements\n\n- **Implementation Roadmap**: 4-phase development plan\n- **Behavior Examples**: Real-world scenarios with expected outcomes\n- **Testing Strategy**: Unit, integration, and chaos test plans\n- **References**: Links to relevant Elasticsearch source files\n\n**Key Design Principles**:\n1. Non-intrusive - integrates without major refactoring\n2. Composable - works alongside existing deciders\n3. Configurable - allows operator control and tuning\n4. Observable - clear logging and explain API output\n5. Safe - graceful degradation without data loss\n\n### 2. **PriorityShardsAllocator.java** - Skeleton Implementation\n\nA Java class implementing the `ShardsAllocator` interface that:\n\n- **Wraps BalancedShardsAllocator**: Delegates actual balancing decisions\n- **Sorts Shards by Priority**: Reorders unassigned shards queue (highest priority first)\n- **Supports Async Allocation**: Implements both sync and async allocation methods\n- **Dynamic Configuration**: Watches for runtime setting changes\n- **Graceful Error Handling**: Continues with standard allocation on errors\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `allocate(RoutingAllocation)` - sorts shards then delegates\n- `allocate(RoutingAllocation, ActionListener<Void>)` - async variant\n- `sortUnassignedShardsByPriority()` - reorders shard queue\n- `getIndexPriority()` - extracts priority from index metadata\n- `isNodePremiumTier()` - classifies node as premium/standard\n\n**Settings Exposed**:\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.enabled` (Boolean, default: true)\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.premium_tiers` (List[String], default: [\"premium\"])\n- `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.threshold` (Integer 0-100, default: 70)\n\n### 3. **PriorityAllocationDecider.java** - Skeleton Implementation\n\nA Java class extending `AllocationDecider` that:\n\n- **Enforces Priority Constraints**: Returns YES/THROTTLE/NO based on priority and tier\n- **Decision Logic**:\n  - High-priority shard on premium node \u2192 YES\n  - High-priority shard on standard node \u2192 THROTTLE (soft constraint)\n  - Low-priority shard on any node \u2192 YES\n- **Composes with Other Deciders**: Fails fast on NO from other deciders\n- **Dynamic Configuration**: Watches for runtime setting changes\n- **Detailed Logging**: Trace-level logging for debugging allocation decisions\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `canAllocate(ShardRouting, RoutingNode, RoutingAllocation)` - main decision logic\n- `canRemain()` - uses same logic as canAllocate\n- `getIndexPriority()` - extracts priority from index metadata\n- `isNodePremiumTier()` - classifies node tier\n\n**Settings Exposed**:\n- Same as PriorityShardsAllocator\n\n## Architecture Diagram\n\n```\nAllocationService (orchestration)\n    \u2193\nShardsAllocator (pluggable)\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 BalancedShardsAllocator (existing)\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 PriorityShardsAllocator (NEW)\n            \u2193\n        [reorder shards by priority]\n            \u2193\n        BalancedShardsAllocator.allocate()\n            \u2193\n        AllocationDeciders chain\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 EnableAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 DiskThresholdDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 AwarenessAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 FilterAllocationDecider\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 PriorityAllocationDecider (NEW)\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 ... other deciders ...\n```\n\n## Design Highlights\n\n### 1. Uses return Decision.YES, Decision.THROTTLE, or Decision.NO\n\n2. **Decision Logic**\n   ```\n   if feature disabled:\n       return YES (always allow)\n\n   if priority < threshold:\n       return YES (no constraint)\n\n   if priority >= threshold:\n       if node is premium:\n           return YES (preferred allocation)\n       else:\n           return THROTTLE (allow but prefer premium)\n   ```\n\n3. **Configuration Settings**\n   - 1. WRITE /workspace/design_doc.md
# Priority-Based Shard Allocation Strategy Design

## Executive Summary

This document describes the design of a new `PriorityShardsAllocator` component for Elasticsearch that extends the existing shard allocation framework to support **priority-aware allocation**. The allocator enables critical indices to be preferentially placed on faster (higher-capacity or better-performing) nodes within the cluster.

---

## 1. Current Architecture Overview

### 1.1 Existing Allocation Framework

Elasticsearch's shard allocation is based on a **pluggable architecture** with three core components:

#### **ShardsAllocator Interface**
- **Location**: `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/allocator/ShardsAllocator.java`
- **Responsibilities**:
  - `allocate(RoutingAllocation)` - Main allocation method
  - `allocate(RoutingAllocation, ActionListener<Void>)` - Async variant
  - `decideShardAllocation(ShardRouting, RoutingAllocation)` - Explain API support
  - `execute(RoutingAllocation, AllocationCommands, ...)` - Execute explicit commands

#### **BalancedShardsAllocator**
- **Location**: `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/allocator/BalancedShardsAllocator.java`
- **Current Implementation**: Balances shards using weighted function approach
- **Balance Factors**:
  - Shard count balance (cluster.routing.allocation.balance.shard)
  - Index spread balance (cluster.routing.allocation.balance.index)
  - Write load balance (cluster.routing.allocation.balance.write_load)
  - Disk usage balance (cluster.routing.allocation.balance.disk_usage)
- **Design Pattern**: Uses WeightFunction to compute node scores; allocates to node with highest score

#### **AllocationDeciders Composition**
- **Location**: `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsear
... (truncated)

# Priority-Based Shard Allocation Strategy for Elasticsearch

## Overview

This directory contains the design and skeleton implementation for a **priority-based shard allocation strategy** for Elasticsearch v8.17.0. The design enables critical indices to be preferentially placed on faster (premium-tier) nodes while maintaining graceful degradation when premium capacity is exhausted.

## Deliverables

### 1. **design_doc.md** - Comprehensive Design Document

A complete design specification covering:

- **Current Architecture Overview**: Detailed analysis of existing allocation framework
  - ShardsAllocator interface and BalancedShardsAllocator implementation
  - AllocationDecider base class and composition pattern
  - Existing decider examples (DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider)

- **Problem Statement**: Why priority-aware allocation is needed
  - Current lack of performance-tier awareness
  - Limitation in handling critical vs. non-critical indices

- **Proposed Design**: Four-component solution
  - `index.routing.allocation.priority` setting (0-100, default 50)
  - `node.attr.allocation_tier` attribute (e.g., "premium", "standard")
  - `PriorityAllocationDecider` - enforces priority constraints
  - `PriorityShardsAllocator` - reorders shards by priority for allocation

- **Integration Points**: How new components compose with existing allocation framework
  - Placement in the decider chain
  - Interaction with DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider, FilterAllocationDecider
  - Backward compatibility and graceful degradation

- **API Specification**: New settings and configuration
  - Index settings: `index.routing.allocation.priority`
  - Cluster settings: `cluster.routing.allocation.priority.*`
  - Cluster Explain API enhancements

- **Impleme
... (truncated)

## Deliverable #1: Comprehensive Design Document
**File**: `design_doc.md` (587 lines)

### Contents:
1. **Executive Summary** - High-level overview of the priority-based allocation feature
2. **Current Architecture Overview** (Section 1)
   - Detailed analysis of ShardsAllocator interface
   - BalancedShardsAllocator implementation strategy
   - AllocationDeciders composition pattern
   - Examples: DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider

3. **Problem Statement & Goals** (Section 2)
   - Current limitations in Elasticsearch allocation
   - Desired capabilities for priority-aware placement
   - Design goals: non-intrusive, composable, configurable, observable, safe

4. **Proposed Design** (Section 3) - Four-component solution:
   - **Index Setting**: `index.routing.allocation.priority` (0-100, default 50)
   - **Node Attribute**: `node.attr.allocation_tier` (e.g., "premium", "standard")
   - **PriorityAllocationDecider**: Enforces priority constraints via Decision objects
   - **PriorityShardsAllocator**: Reorders shard queue for priority-first allocation

5. **Integration with Existing Components** (Section 4)
   - Placement in the decider chain
   - Interaction patterns with DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider
   - Graceful degradation when premium capacity exhausted

6. **API Changes & Configuration** (Section 5)
   - New index setting for priority
   - New cluster settings for feature control
   - Cluster Explain API enhancements
   - Configuration examples with YAML/JSON

7. **Implementation Roadmap** (Section 6)
   - 4-phase development plan (Foundat
